<div id="review_87208105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87208105" />
    <a title="Darcy Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852193-darcy-stewart"><img alt="Darcy Stewart" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87208105?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darcy Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darcy Stewart" href="/user/show/1852193-darcy-stewart">Darcy Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87208105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10171410411592950001">Strange Power<br/>This is a very good book. The the vampire in this book ix very different. He doesn't suck blood, he sucks energy. All of the characters are very interesting. The book involves plenty of evil. The students really start to notice something terribly wrong. The book ends in a nice clip hanger. I couldn't put this book done. This is the first L.J. Smith novel I have read. I really think a lot of people will like this. I certainly recommend this to everyone. Kaitlyn is a nice girl that te</span>
  <span id="freeText10171410411592950001" style="display:none">Strange Power<br />This is a very good book. The the vampire in this book ix very different. He doesn't suck blood, he sucks energy. All of the characters are very interesting. The book involves plenty of evil. The students really start to notice something terribly wrong. The book ends in a nice clip hanger. I couldn't put this book done. This is the first L.J. Smith novel I have read. I really think a lot of people will like this. I certainly recommend this to everyone. Kaitlyn is a nice girl that tends to run into a lot more trouble then everyone else. I thought it so romantic that Gabriel rescues her from the guy at the airport who shows up at the house. I'm surprised the grown-ups let the kids do whatever they want. The adults are very strange. Something is terribly wrong with the place and the people working there. Kaitlyn liked two of the guys involved in the experiments. Gabriel seems to dangerous. They all need to find help. The truths are hidden by lies. Lewis cares way too much to much about objects. He's so oblivious to everything going on around him. Many things start to unravel. You start wondering what the experiments are for, how the kids are going to manage their powers, and terrible evil lurking in the house. I think it is quite funny that Zetes have two small nasty dogs. They hardly seem real. The author makes you hate these dogs more than anything.<br />The Possessed<br />This was another great book of series. A lot of things happen in this book. There is a lot of suspense. The students are trying to escape Mr. Zetes the man who is trying to turn them into weapons or kill them. This one is better than first. I definitely recommend reading this one. The students show up at the house of protection and learn many secrets. They learn about their race and the mysterious crystal. They also are attacked by other people of their own race. Join them in the escape from Mr. Zetes. <br />The Passion<br />I really loved this book. The ending is perfect. Some of it you expect but some of it you don't. At first I though tit would be another vampire novel but it isn't. This is great for any teen to read who really likes fantasy. The book shows some evil, but it just briefly touches it. The book has some tense moments in it. I couldn't put this book down. I found this to be very exciting. LJ Smith has gotten me to read everything she has written. I didn't find a moment of dullness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10171410411592950001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_111609012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111609012" />
    <a title="Talulah Mankiller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3245656-talulah-mankiller"><img alt="Talulah Mankiller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285385665p2/3245656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111609012?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Talulah Mankiller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Talulah Mankiller" href="/user/show/3245656-talulah-mankiller">Talulah Mankiller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111609012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3235407256180412546">Psychic boarding school goes horribly, horribly wrong!<br/><br/>Seriously, people. Haven’t y’all ever read Lois Duncan’s Down a Dark Hall? If you have psychic powers and someone offers you a scholarship, RUN FOR THE FUCKING HILLS!<br/><br/>Ahem. It never goes well. It’s always part of some government experiment/corporate money-making scheme/WHO THE FUCK CARES, JUST FUCKING RUN ALREADY. Really. By this point, accepting an invitation to attend one of these schools is like running UPstairs in a horror movie: everyone </span>
  <span id="freeText3235407256180412546" style="display:none">Psychic boarding school goes horribly, horribly wrong!<br /><br />Seriously, people. Haven’t y’all ever read Lois Duncan’s Down a Dark Hall? If you have psychic powers and someone offers you a scholarship, RUN FOR THE FUCKING HILLS!<br /><br />Ahem. It never goes well. It’s always part of some government experiment/corporate money-making scheme/WHO THE FUCK CARES, JUST FUCKING RUN ALREADY. Really. By this point, accepting an invitation to attend one of these schools is like running UPstairs in a horror movie: everyone in the audience is screaming, “JESUS CHRIST, HAVEN’T YOU EVER SEEN SCREAM BEFORE?!”<br /><br />So yeah. Besides the whole “wow, this premise is really tired” part, L.J. Smith continues to have squicky race issues. On the one hand, non-white characters finally get some action! On the other hand, said action only happens when the main girl has gone on to her real true love, leaving her first love in need of some comfort. Also, have I mentioned the fact that there’s an Asian male character, who gets like, zero plot time and whom the heroine automatically deems “safe” and “non-threatening” because he’s “so small”?<br /><br />UGH.<br /><br />Yeah, and Smith can’t go two seconds without reminding us that the Native American girl is, in fact, Native American and all in touch with nature and shit. Y’all, one day I’m going to write a story starring a Native American woman who drives a fucking hummer and bulldozes down a forest to put in a swimming pool. THAT IS HOW TIRED I AM OF THIS STEREOTYPE.<br /><br />Dear L.J. Smith: if you cannot write nonwhite characters without being RIDICULOUSLY offensive, how’s about you go get some racial sensitivity training? That, or set your books somewhere really, really white so we don’t have to deal with this nonsense from you anymore. We’d all be real grateful.<br /><br />Recommended for: Skip!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3235407256180412546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64119011" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64119011" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/778585-k"><img alt="K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268284260p2/778585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64119011?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/778585-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671023300" href="/book/show/293980.The_Strange_Power_The_Possessed_The_Passion">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64119011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16923372451195606815">Dark Visions is another book which includes 3 stories: The Strange Power, The Possessed, and The Passion. As I have found Smith's books to be hot and cold, I was nervous about this one, but was determined to read it anyways as the subject matter interested me. And... I was pleasantly suprised to find that I loved it. By that, I mean the stories interested me so much that I couldn't put it down due to having to see how things worked out in the end. Trust me when I say no one could be more suprise</span>
  <span id="freeText16923372451195606815" style="display:none">Dark Visions is another book which includes 3 stories: The Strange Power, The Possessed, and The Passion. As I have found Smith's books to be hot and cold, I was nervous about this one, but was determined to read it anyways as the subject matter interested me. And... I was pleasantly suprised to find that I loved it. By that, I mean the stories interested me so much that I couldn't put it down due to having to see how things worked out in the end. Trust me when I say no one could be more suprised by this than I am. Unlike the 3 books in the NightWorld series, I enjoyed all the stories and their characters. I found myself drawn to the story, and found the little plot twists suprising and unexpected. After reading this book, I will probably be more likely to give this author a chance. And for those of you who may be laughing at me, an adult, liking a book meant for a YA audience, all I have to say is don't knock it until you tried it. Besides, we all have our guilty pleasures. If it isn't obvious by now, I would defiantely recommend this book to other readers, young adults and adults alike.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16923372451195606815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15330073365883978916">Excellent book. Perfect for a nice escape from reality, a nice because it wasn't another vampire book. A bit lacking in character and relationship development. We never get to see the viewpoint of 2 of the 5 main characters, so motives and ties are a bit unclear. The other point that I didn't think matched up was Kaitlyn's relationship wit LeShan. Her only contact with him in two books is him attacking her, then suddenly in the third he's no longer an enemy, but Kait isn't sure she likes him ver</span>
  <span id="freeText15330073365883978916" style="display:none">Excellent book. Perfect for a nice escape from reality, a nice because it wasn't another vampire book. A bit lacking in character and relationship development. We never get to see the viewpoint of 2 of the 5 main characters, so motives and ties are a bit unclear. The other point that I didn't think matched up was Kaitlyn's relationship wit LeShan. Her only contact with him in two books is him attacking her, then suddenly in the third he's no longer an enemy, but Kait isn't sure she likes him very much, and the next thing you hear from LeShan, he's dead and Kait is mourning his death and going into shock and treating his death as if it were Gabriel's or Rob's. <br />Aside from the few unclarities, the characters are the kind you love and hate, in a good way. The plot is good, though I REALLY recommend reading all the books together, like in the combination set. Otherwise the second book may get a tad slow.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9101327763902809777">L J. Smith’s version of psychic YA story, Dark Visions contents three books: The Strange Power, The Possessed, The Passion. Basically it’s a story of good psychic teenagers with special abilities fighting the evil boss who wanted to use their abilities to make ton of money. AGAIN there’s a love triangle in the book but this one is OK, most of the main characters are also likable. <br/><br/>The only problem I have with the story is when those ‘bad’ psychic kids(who help the evil boss) show up, they were pr</span>
  <span id="freeText9101327763902809777" style="display:none">L J. Smith’s version of psychic YA story, Dark Visions contents three books: The Strange Power, The Possessed, The Passion. Basically it’s a story of good psychic teenagers with special abilities fighting the evil boss who wanted to use their abilities to make ton of money. AGAIN there’s a love triangle in the book but this one is OK, most of the main characters are also likable. <br /><br />The only problem I have with the story is when those ‘bad’ psychic kids(who help the evil boss) show up, they were presented as your typical make-up wearing, untidy and rock n’ roll loving bad kids, while the good kids are the wholesome, clean-cut, all-American middle class/lower middle class kids. ARGH the stereotype. *sighs*</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254024390?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AZVP " class="user" itemprop="url" name="AZVP " href="/user/show/7099610-azvp">AZVP </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7099610-azvp?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7099610-azvp?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7099610-azvp?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254024390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3533557472042703871"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“She stood slim and proud as some medieval witch princess against the dawn.” (p.536)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>This book has been staring at me for years, taunting me. I’ve tried reading it before but I couldn’t make myself read past the first book. Luckily after four years I’ve finally forced myself to read it cover to cover. <br/><br/><u>Summary:</u> This series followed Kaitlyn, Gabriel, Rob, Anna and Lewis, a group of psychic teenagers that were gathered in the Zetes Institute so that they could learn to control their powe</span>
  <span id="freeText3533557472042703871" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“She stood slim and proud as some medieval witch princess against the dawn.” (p.536)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>This book has been staring at me for years, taunting me. I’ve tried reading it before but I couldn’t make myself read past the first book. Luckily after four years I’ve finally forced myself to read it cover to cover. <br><br><u>Summary:</u> This series followed Kaitlyn, Gabriel, Rob, Anna and Lewis, a group of psychic teenagers that were gathered in the Zetes Institute so that they could learn to control their powers. However, things weren’t what they seemed in the Institute. When intentions were revealed, the group found themselves psychically linked and struggling to stay alive. <br><br>A series about psychic kids that fight against an evil mastermind that wants to exploit their powers should be an interesting read. Unfortunately the series as a whole was boring. The villain was obvious from the moment he was presented and was the most clichéd character of the bunch. The parts that were supposed to be intense and heart pounding were dull and short. This was basically my reading experience: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399474279ra/9556435.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>The Characters:</u> <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“You don’t invite the local witch to parties. No matter how beautiful she is.” (p.1)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Kaitlyn Fairchild was the “witch” from Ohio. Since she was a child Kait had been an outcast due to her strange ringed eyes and her ability to predict the future through her drawings. Kait had a negative opinion of men ever since she dated this <i>one</i> guy who refused to go out with her in public. She then decided that <i>all</i> men were scum who were only interested in sex. That, of course, changed when she got to the Institute and met Rob. Her opinion changed so fast it gave me whiplash. What happened to the “Three sloppy, meaty-handed, too-big-to-control, hormone-crazed Power Rangers.” (p.30) Kait? She forgot over the sounds of them praising her to high heavens. She was stubborn, prideful and somewhat unstable, but mostly unbearably annoying. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“A very masculine presence−if Anna was a cool wind, this boy was a golden solar flare.” (p.39)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Rob Kessler, the golden boy from North Carolina. He had the ability to heal people by manipulating their life energy. At the beginning of the series Rob didn’t know what girls were for due to an accident. But of course Kaitlyn’s specialness cured him of that.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405566308ra/10416014.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He was a good southern boy, he respected authority and was polite to females. Of course he also knew Gabriel from the other research facility he was in, and of course he hated him. He was as interesting as white bread and such a goodie goodie it was irritating more often than not. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“He was startlingly handsome−but there was a cold wariness in his face and movements.” (p.45)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Gabriel Wolfe, the bad boy telepath who committed murder, a.k.a. the only character I actually cared about. He was perpetually snarling/baring his teeth/smiling disturbingly. Gabriel was the other part of the love triangle, the black hole to Rob’s sun. He hated Rob since they were in the research facility and more so after he realized he had feelings for Kait. Gabriel was the ambiguous character in the series, so his loyalties jumped around. I think I liked him since he didn’t like Rob. Even though he was an unreasonable ass from time to time, he wasn’t stupid enough to trust people immediately and he found a way−albeit mostly illegal−to get a task done. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Peacefulness seemed to come from the other girl like a cool wind.” (p.34)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Anna Eva Whiteraven was the Native American with the power to influence animals. She was just there so Kaitlyn could have a girl to talk to about guys. Her involvement in the plot was minimal at best, I think she only used her power like twice. It also annoyed me that most of the descriptions that were associated with the girl included the words: calming, serene, peaceful or other synonyms. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her romance with Rob in the last book bothered me as much as Kait’s since they barely interact with each other throughout the series. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“He wasn’t big and gross, but rather small and neat.” (p.35)</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Then there was Lewis Chao, the other character who was just there. The Asian-American from San Francisco who had psychokinesis but barely used it. He was helpful every once in a while, which was more than I could say about Anna.<br> <br><u>The Romance:</u><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“She would never have believed she could fall in love on one day’s acquaintance. But there it was. And every minute she was around Rob, the feeling grew stronger.” (p.85).</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>I didn't like the romance at all. Kaitlyn fell in love with Rob after knowing him for twenty-four hours. <i>A day!</i> They hadn't even had a full conversation yet. When I read that I had to put the book down for a moment.<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398626124ra/9442791.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Every time Kait went on about how much she loved Rob I wanted to jump into the book and slap her. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405563723ra/10415704.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her relationship with Gabriel was <i>way</i> more believable. They actually interacted and she gradually started to care about him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><u>The Verdict:</u><br>I wouldn’t recommend this series. The plot was boring, the romance was cheesy and the characters aren’t compelling. <br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3533557472042703871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_111993383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111993383" />
    <a title="Milly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4000502-milly"><img alt="Milly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291008553p2/4000502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111993383?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milly" href="/user/show/4000502-milly">Milly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4000502-milly?shelf=psychics">psychics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111993383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3584635785130403918">Books by L.J. Smith are a hit and miss for me. I love her Night World and Secret Circle series but didn't care much for her Vampire Diaries even though they are her most popular books right now. The last series I read of hers was so-so for me as well. But despite that, there was no reluctance from me in picking this book up because it's thematically different. The book focuses on teenagers with psychic abilities rather than your usual run-off-the-mill vampire-werewolves-faeries plot lines. It wa</span>
  <span id="freeText3584635785130403918" style="display:none">Books by L.J. Smith are a hit and miss for me. I love her Night World and Secret Circle series but didn't care much for her Vampire Diaries even though they are her most popular books right now. The last series I read of hers was so-so for me as well. But despite that, there was no reluctance from me in picking this book up because it's thematically different. The book focuses on teenagers with psychic abilities rather than your usual run-off-the-mill vampire-werewolves-faeries plot lines. It was a breath of fresh air and a nice change of pace to read this book. <br /><br />The story is written in Kaitlyn's point of view. She's a senior in high school and an outcast in her hometown due to her witch-like eyes and her ability to have premonitions of impeding deaths through her drawings. Her ability has frightened others thinking she truly is a witch. When the opportunity to leave town, attend a different high school and get a scholarship to college of her picking was presented to her, Kaitlyn took it and came to California to become a part of a group of kids with psychic abilities who were to be studied to teach them to control their abilities. There she meets 4 other interesting teens with cool psychic powers and truly find out the reason why they are all there. And so the plot thickens...<br /><br />The other psychics: Rob the healer, Lewis with psychokinesis, Anna who can speak to animals, and Gabriel the telepath and the only one with the ability to suck other people's energies and abilities and potentially kill. Gabriel also has the ability to connect all 5 of them and communicate with each other through their minds, proving quite useful later as the fight ensues between good and evil powers. Other psychics are also introduced later on and make-up the dark and evil psychics who were used to murder and rob. <br /><br />With the realization of her potential and finally having friends and people that care for her and she cares for back, Kaitlyn becomes empowered and comes out the clear leader of the group as she is the only one who can seem to tame Gabriel, the most powerful and deadly psychic of the group. To spice things up, Kaitlyn gets herself entangled in a love triangle between the exceptionally good and righteous Rob and the dark and mysterious Gabriel. Despite her strong attraction for Rob, Kaitlyn can't help but be intrigued by Gabriel. Can't resist the bad boy. Can't resist the urge to take care of poor 'ol Gabriel who's tortured inside. Can't help wanting to help him find his inner goodness and help him change for the better. I know, we can't help it. We want to change men because they don't know what's good for them. Women can't help it. It's the maternal instinct kicking in. <br /><br />Although predictable, the long ride to the end was fun and entertaining. It was packed with action sequences page after page. Though we know who the leading characters are, Smith did a wonderful job making each character stand out. Their group was only strong when they worked as a team, clearly and distinctly showing what each psychic of the group contributed and how each reinforced the strength of the other. <br /><br />The story about the crystal and the existence of another world was quite intriguing and very creative. It was a nice infusion of ingenious.<br /><br />Reading this story was a nice experience. It wasn't mind blowing but interesting enough to keep me wanting for more L.J. Smith books! It makes me wish I had powers too! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3584635785130403918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_102418991" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102418991" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102418991?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=for-review-read">for-review-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102418991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16071065355911438820">Kaitlyn has always been considered an outsider at her school and is known as a witch because of her strange drawings. When she gets the urge to draw she never knows what she will produce but her pictures always give a warning about something that will happen in the future. When she is offered a place at an institute for gifted psychics she jumps at the chance to go to California and hopes to find out more about her gifts. Life at the institute isn't what she was expecting though. She makes 4 new</span>
  <span id="freeText16071065355911438820" style="display:none">Kaitlyn has always been considered an outsider at her school and is known as a witch because of her strange drawings. When she gets the urge to draw she never knows what she will produce but her pictures always give a warning about something that will happen in the future. When she is offered a place at an institute for gifted psychics she jumps at the chance to go to California and hopes to find out more about her gifts. Life at the institute isn't what she was expecting though. She makes 4 new friends who all have different psychic abilities but all is not what it seems and someone at the institute seems to want to use the students for their own agenda. When the group accidentally get locked together in a telepathic link they are desperate to find a way to break the connection between them. But as time goes on they realise that the link between them may be the only way they will survive long enough to figure out what is really going on at the institute.<br /><br />I really enjoyed L.J. Smith's Night World series so was looking forward to trying her Dark Visions trilogy. I love the fact that all 3 stories have been incorporated into 1 volume so there is no having to wait between installments. Dark Visions was a great read and I would definitely recommend the series to fans of young adult urban fantasy.<br /><br />Each of the students that have been hand picked to attend the institute have different psychic abilities. I'm not going to tell you what they are - you'll have to read the book if you want to find out - but I found it interesting to see how their abilities worked and the impact that had on them as individuals and as a group. Kaitlyn had always felt different from her peers so meeting others with similar abilities means she finally has people she can relate to. She quickly forms friendships with Anna, Lewis and Rob but Gabriel holds himself apart from the group and is harder to get to know. I liked all of the characters but I'd have to say Gabriel was my favorite, it takes time to get to know him but he will steal your heart as you do.<br /><br />The psychic bond that formed between them allowed them to read each others thoughts and made life very difficult as everyone could hear what the others were thinking, I don't think I'd like to be stuck in a bond like that even with my closest friends. The only one who could keep his thoughts to himself was Gabriel who has a very strong telepathic ability and is the one who caused the bond to form in the first place. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the romance in the story, Kaitlyn is attracted to both Rob and Gabriel. They are practically complete opposites but you can see what it is about each of them that draws her to them. Rob is kind and caring while Gabriel is the secretive bad boy that leaves you wanting to know more. I thought the romance between them developed well and I'll just say that I was happy with the ending.<br /><br />As much as I love having so many stories about vampires and other supernatural characters available Dark Visions was a refreshing change and I'm looking forward to reading more by L.J. Smith. I'd definitely recommend giving this book a try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16071065355911438820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Amanda J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5381770-amanda-j"><img alt="Amanda J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306031788p2/5381770.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer170062015" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12951490259821410920">This book was sexy and suspenseful! L.J always finds a way to create the perfect heroin and hasn't yet to disappoint!<br/> This story is about Kaitlyn Fairchild, a girl with fiery hair to match her temper, and a pair of haunting witch eyes to go with her prophetic drawings to earn her the top spot as an outsider and freak in her home town. They all consider her a witch, but she isn't; she's a psychic. Kaitlyn can't wait for college and finally leave high school at the end of the year, but everything </span>
  <span id="freeText12951490259821410920" style="display:none">This book was sexy and suspenseful! L.J always finds a way to create the perfect heroin and hasn't yet to disappoint!<br /> This story is about Kaitlyn Fairchild, a girl with fiery hair to match her temper, and a pair of haunting witch eyes to go with her prophetic drawings to earn her the top spot as an outsider and freak in her home town. They all consider her a witch, but she isn't; she's a psychic. Kaitlyn can't wait for college and finally leave high school at the end of the year, but everything is put on hold when Joyce shows up at school and Kait accepts the invitation to the Zetes institute of Physic Studies. Here she can get a fresh start and study with other psychic teens to learn how to control their powers. At the institute Kaitlyn meets Rob. The model southern golden boy and not shy of gorgeous, he uses his powers to heal others with his psychic energy, he's kind and gorgeous with his golden hair and eyes to match he's warm and inviting, but completely clueless when it comes to girls. Kaitlyn quickly finds her self falling for the all-american boy, and then she meets Gabriel. Completely opposite of rob, he's definitely not the boy next door. With striking features, black shaggy hair, and opaque black eyes, he's dangerously beautiful; and it's not just an act. Gabriel is also aggressive and mysterious, a telepath with the true nature of a psychic vampire; feeding off other peoples life force. Together, with Rob and Gabriel's history and opposing forces, they begin to threaten the stability of the group. Then one of the experiments goes wrong, trapping the five teens into a psychic link. It soon starts to threaten all the members sanities and even their lives. And Kaitlyn must decide whom to trust, and whom to love.<br /><br />This book was fantastic! There's a love triangle with Rob, Kait, and Gabriel, and also forbidden love and tuns and tuns of action! 5 stars! L.J always succeeds to create the perfect bad boy and then the perfect way to redeem himself to make him worthy for the girl! This book gave me every emotion to rage, to excitement, to horror, to love. I would definitely recommend this book to anyone who likes L.J Smith's work, or any romance or fantasy novels! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12951490259821410920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138372956" />
    <a title="Halinor Everdeen Cipriano " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4449588-halinor-everdeen-cipriano"><img alt="Halinor Everdeen Cipriano " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298034434p2/4449588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138372956?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Halinor Everdeen Cipriano " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Halinor Everdeen Cipriano " href="/user/show/4449588-halinor-everdeen-cipriano">Halinor Everdeen Cipriano </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416989561" href="/book/show/6322323-dark-visions">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138372956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18211186636641707752">I've read a whole Christmas turkey sized load of reviews that say the protagonist in this scummy excuse for a book has depth and a unique, macho character that sets her apart from the other fourteen million heroins who supposedly are the epitome of bravery courage and goodness knows what other load of bull! None of the characters besides Gabriel Wolfe had any depth or development intensifying since the get go... And yes Kaitlyn we do know that you were mistreated for your strange (yet exceedingl</span>
  <span id="freeText18211186636641707752" style="display:none">I've read a whole Christmas turkey sized load of reviews that say the protagonist in this scummy excuse for a book has depth and a unique, macho character that sets her apart from the other fourteen million heroins who supposedly are the epitome of bravery courage and goodness knows what other load of bull! None of the characters besides Gabriel Wolfe had any depth or development intensifying since the get go... And yes Kaitlyn we do know that you were mistreated for your strange (yet exceedingly alluring, and not to mention very soulful)eyes! You specified that the first two hundred pages of the book! Basically there is no assertiveness in Kaitlyn's character besides she's a loner and depends so heavily on poor Rob, that I'm surprised the poor guy didn't get a migraine... but alas! Of course he had to be the angelic illuminated soul that stayed daft throughout and experienced no stimulating change, though the author presumes that he changed since he fell in love with Kaitlyn... (and considering how air headed she is, and how intelligent he was supposed to be, that is quite the change!) The other two kids (besides Gabriel) are present for the sake of additional stowaways...some characters, are barely present and can be ignored all together... therefore as a conclusion I would like to say that if you insist on reading the book... then read it for the only poignant, pleasantly present character Gabriel.... and the unquenchable acerbic thirst of Mr. Z.... but mostly just Gabriel... he's hot! </span>
  <a data-text-id="18211186636641707752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QmPlVlRtRmGhy4cgacgOkyDt9Xd1x6f4K8NYY6sCE26ryn4zbqU0OWlQsfQSmuBvmYsBZ6EyULOdCaJMAr23WQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('e7/vvYcCXRvDkmVdfNg/dcz/f98n7EP/2u9DmqDTn4WSFnTYvcovQwsJU4kHitGJdZmLz/MZtLRsJbm1CWw7sg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15822094562697892954">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series'>https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br/><br/><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in th</span>
  <span id="freeText15822094562697892954" style="display:none">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series">https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br /><br /><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in the Bay Area of California, with a backyard that is full of flowers, which she adores, especially with many different shades of roses.<br /><br />She loves to visit a friend's little cabin in the Point Reyes National Seashore area, which has lots of trees, lots of animals, lots of beaches to walk on, and lots of places to hike. Once, while hiking, she saw a snow-white buck which allowed her to follow it nearly half a mile. She also likes to collect things: angels (they remind her of her late mother), tiny boxes from different countries or of fanciful shape, nineteenth century children's literature, and books about quantum physics--especially about the mystery of the dark energy in the universe. A militant optimist, she is also part of the Velociraptor Sisterhood (a fancy way of saying that she likes to read, write and discuss books with strong female characters), and she has traveled extensively in Europe and the Far East. The two countries she loves to visit most are Great Britain, with its historic monuments and amazing country landscapes, and Japan, with its bustling urban life and exquisite mountain scenery.<br /><br />Her favorite current writer is Terry Pratchett, the author of the Discworld series, for its wild and witty satires on life, death, war, love, assassins, coppers, and Australia. Her favorite classical writer is Jane Austen. Her favorite poets are Robert Frost and Emily Dickinson. Her favorite movies are The Seven Samurai and Avatar (analyze that!). She doesn't have a favorite TV show, because she doesn't have time to watch TV (and only owns one for playing movies).<br /><br />Her favorite people are her readers, each of whom she cherishes with deep and lasting affection.<br /><br /><i>Note: L. J. Smith wrote books 1-7 of The Vampire Diaries series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. wrote books 1-3 of The Secret Circle series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. did not write any of the Originals or Stefan's Diaries. These were written by Kevin Williamson and/or various ghostwritters.</i> <br /></span>
